  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer10218179303197047864"><i>My name - my True Name - is Ashallayn’ darkmyr Tallyn. I am the last remaining son of Mab, Queen of the Unseelie Court. And I am dead to her.   <span id="freeText10218179303197047864" style="display:none"><i>My name - my True Name - is Ashallayn’ darkmyr Tallyn. I am the last remaining son of Mab, Queen of the Unseelie Court. And I am dead to her. My fall began, as many stories do, with a girl…</i><p>To cold faery prince Ash, love was a weakness for mortals and fools. His own love had died a horrible death, killing any gentler feelings the Winter prince might have had. Or so he thought.</p><p>Then Meghan Chase - a half human, half fey slip of a girl - smashed through his barricades, binding him to her irrevocably with his oath to be her knight. And when all of Faery nearly fell to the Iron fey, she severed their bond to save his life. Meghan is now the Iron Queen, ruler of a realm where no Winter or Summer fey can survive.</p><p>With the unwelcome company of his archrival, Summer Court prankster Puck, and the infuriating cait sith Grimalkin, Ash begins a journey he is bound to see through to its end - a quest to find a way to honor his vow to stand by Meghan's side.</p><p>To survive in the Iron Realm, Ash must have a soul and a mortal body. But the tests he must face to earn these things are impossible. And along the way Ash learns something that changes everything. A truth that challenges his darkest beliefs and shows him that, sometimes, it takes more than courage to make the ultimate sacrifice.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="10218179303197047864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[
  var timer_314130_end_at = 1861629 + new Date().getTime()/1000;

  function timer_314130_updateTimer() {
    var time_left = "";
    var secs_left = timer_314130_end_at - new Date().getTime()/1000;

    if(secs_left <= 0) {
      document.getElementById("timer_314130").innerHTML = "closed";
      clearInterval(timer_314130_updater);
      return;
    }

    var minutes_left = secs_left / 60;
    var hours_left = minutes_left / 60;
    var days_left = Math.floor(hours_left / 24);

    if(days_left > 0) {
      if(false){
        time_left += days_left + ":";
      }else{
        time_left += days_left + " days and ";
      }
    }
    if(false){
      time_left += Math.floor(hours_left%24/10)
      time_left += Math.floor(hours_left%24)%10 + ":";
    }else{
      time_left += Math.floor(hours_left%24) + ":";
    }
    time_left += Math.floor(minutes_left%60/10);
    time_left += Math.floor(minutes_left%10) + ":";
    time_left += Math.floor(secs_left%60/10);
    time_left += Math.floor(secs_left%10);

    document.getElementById("timer_314130").innerHTML = time_left;
  }

  timer_314130_updateTimer();
  var timer_314130_updater = setInterval(timer_314130_updateTimer, 100);
//]]>
</script>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This is techincally the last book in ‘the iron fey’, and so it is - the last book telling of Meghan, Ash, Puck, and their adventures. However, there a<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This is techincally the last book in ‘the iron fey’, and so it is - the last book telling of Meghan, Ash, Puck, and their adventures. However, there are three more books afterwards, a trilogy - ‘the iron fey: call of the forgotten’. These are from a different person’s point of view, and set quite a few years after the iron knight.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_129923684" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129923684" />
    <a title="Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten"><img alt="Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305870184p2/2406353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129923684?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)" href="/user/show/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten">Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=harlequin-sent">harlequin-sent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=publisher-sent">publisher-sent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=signed-copies">signed-copies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer129923684&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129923684" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12337219336828803571"><b>**Read in October 2011**</b><br/><br/><i>***Firstly, thank-you to Harlequin Teen Australia for sending me a copy to read and review**</i><br/><br/>The Iron Knight marks a dramatic conclusion to Julie Kagawa’s Iron Fey series. Weaving together all the beauty and wonder that has made this series so captivating, The Iron Knight explores the darkest places of the Nevernever as Ash faces truths, challenges and revelations in his quest for a soul; racing towards a climax that will leave you breathless!<br/><br/>In all honestly I’m saddened t</span>
  <span id="freeText12337219336828803571" style="display:none"><b>**Read in October 2011**</b><br /><br /><i>***Firstly, thank-you to Harlequin Teen Australia for sending me a copy to read and review**</i><br /><br />The Iron Knight marks a dramatic conclusion to Julie Kagawa’s Iron Fey series. Weaving together all the beauty and wonder that has made this series so captivating, The Iron Knight explores the darkest places of the Nevernever as Ash faces truths, challenges and revelations in his quest for a soul; racing towards a climax that will leave you breathless!<br /><br />In all honestly I’m saddened to see this series come to an end, but I found this book to be a very fitting end to a series that has taken me on highs and lows, through danger and adventure, shown me love and heartbreak and ultimately captured me with each and every book. Julie Kagawa has created a gem right here, with a world and characters beautiful in their own rights and magic when she put them together. Every page, ever book has just gotten better and better and Kagawa proves she can still knock our socks off with more twists and turns, and shocks and revelations than I knew what to do with in this book!<br /><br />There wasn’t a moment during Ash’s adventure that I was bored or able to be dragged away. It was stunning watching as he and Puck travelled far and wide as part of their journey to find Ash a soul. Of course it was fantastic seeing Puck (AKA Robin Goodfellow) return in all his pesky glory, creating more mischief and making me smile even when ten seconds before I’d wanted to cry. Brimming with old friends and new, all of which helped Ash in some way or another, this story takes us into the heart and head of Ash, allowing us a glimpse into the very depth of the Winter Prince. This book is an emotional roller-coaster ride as Ash faces his past in an attempt to find his future. Just when it seemed like we all knew what would happen with this book, Ash is faced with not one, but two equally difficult choices to make in his quest to return to Megan. <br /><br />I really felt for Ash in this book—it was impossible not to, but I feel like he really cemented and proved why he is, and will always be, one of the best male leads in YA fiction. We’ve all known Ash had led a hard life, and had done some horrible things but in this book the reality really sinks in as we see the horrors Ash was a part of and the blood that once stained his hands. We must face the horror of his past with our hero as he attempted to pass his tests and return to his love. I think Ash grew so much in this book and it was brilliant to see. <br />Now I’m not going to go into a lot of detail for fear of giving too much away, but throughout the series we’ve watched Ash morn his lost love, even as he fell for Megan and in Iron Knight Ash faces a revelation and choice I doubt any of us readers ever expected he’d face. Julie Kagawa certainly knows how to pull our heart strings, but in the end Ash made the right decision. We all knew he loved Megan, but by throwing in this twist Kagawa has truly <i>validated</i> their love and proven that it really is the real deal; that it’s stronger than anything else. <br /><br />There were heart-wrenching moments and throughout the whole book you truly do wonder how it will end. Nothing ever seemed safe, even towards the end of the book when everything seemed to come crashing down, before soaring higher and higher than before. <br />There’s been pain and tears, laughter and joy and heart-breaking sorrow, but in this book we finally find the ending we were all searching for as The Iron Fey series comes to a close. As we face the final chapter in what truly has been an incredible series, Kagawa delivers one of the best books and doesn’t disappoint as she ends the series with endless hope and possibilities and I’m sure leaves us all wishing we could get our hands on the spin-off right now.....<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12337219336828803571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2019134137" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2019134137" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2019134137?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12471240-the-iron-knight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=read-listened-with-my-kids">read-listened-with-my-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=age-difference">age-difference</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=childhood-loves">childhood-loves</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2019134137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4294705565975964712">From the time I started listening to this series, I have been unable to pull myself away from it. Over the course of a week or so, I have read the entire series from start to finish. I have enjoyed every minute. (Okay, maybe not all of the time spent discussing Ariella.) Gladly, I can say that this series did not fizzle out at the end like many series do. This story was action-packed and engaging right to the very end.<br/><br/>Picking up where 'The Iron Queen' and 'Summer's Crossing' left off, Ash and Me</span>
  <span id="freeText4294705565975964712" style="display:none">From the time I started listening to this series, I have been unable to pull myself away from it. Over the course of a week or so, I have read the entire series from start to finish. I have enjoyed every minute. (Okay, maybe not all of the time spent discussing Ariella.) Gladly, I can say that this series did not fizzle out at the end like many series do. This story was action-packed and engaging right to the very end.<br /><br />Picking up where 'The Iron Queen' and 'Summer's Crossing' left off, Ash and Meghan are separated for most of this book. He's working diligently to find a way to get back to Meghan's side, even if it means becoming human so that he can survive the Iron Realm. He'll stop at nothing to get back to her.<br /><br />In some ways it was kind of fitting that now that Ash has finally figured out that he loves Meghan that he would be kept apart from her. After all, Meghan endured his cold shoulder treatment repeatedly. So, I kind of felt like most of this book was Ash's dose of karma for how he rebuffed Meghan in 'The Iron Daughter'. (I'm blood-thirsty that way.)<br /><br />I don't want to say too much, but I will say that there were some pretty big twists along the way. I can't say I was completely surprised, but there were definitely some wrenches thrown in the plans. One of my biggest pet peeves - the perfect, dead ex-girlfriend - continued to be an issue in a huge way. (Why can't this dead girl just GO AWAY???) <br /><br />Maybe I should be more sensitive and try to like Ariella, but I just can't. Ash's wishy-washy feelings also got on my nerves where the dead ex was concerned. It made me question the genuineness of his feelings for Meghan. <br /><br />Meanwhile, Puck started looking better and better. The poor guy's loyalty was infallible, but he was destined to forever remain in the "friend-zone". My heart broke for him. <br /><br />As Ash endures multiple trials on his quest to gain a soul and become human, Puck, Grimalkin and the great Wolf hunter are right by his side. Like 'Summer's Crossing', Meghan was absent for a large part of this book. However, the robust cast of characters in 'The Iron Knight' did not leave me wanting the way that the earlier novella did. There was never a dull moment.<br /><br />More so than any of the books that preceded this one, 'The Iron Knight' provided insight into Ash's character. I felt like I really got to know him in this book. I won't lie, he definitely had some pretty big skeletons in his closet. However, in my opinion, he had a soul all along. He clearly had a conscience, even if he was taught to ignore it from the time he was young. <br /><br />I really felt for Ash, especially as a child. His world was so cruel and cold. Never was he nurtured like a child should be. It is a wonder that he didn't turn into a total psychopath.<br /><br />At long last, things worked out the way that they should have. I was left feeling relieved and contented at the end of this book. A part of me was even a little sad that I had reached the end of this series. <br /><br />Overall, this was a fantastic book. It was the perfect finale to this series. I'm glad that I read it and I would definitely recommend it to anyone looking for a "clean" fantasy/adventure/paranormal type of story. It has romance, as well as plenty of action.<br /><br />Check out more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookaddicthaven.com">www.bookaddicthaven.com</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4294705565975964712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_195178609" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195178609" />
    <a title="Sabrina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5771244-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195178609?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina" href="/user/show/5771244-sabrina">Sabrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781459215337" href="/book/show/12418272-the-iron-knight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5771244-sabrina?shelf=series-concluded">series-concluded</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195178609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer566319364711956854">First, let me say that I really enjoyed the previous installments of this series; so I'm not happy to squash this one down. Maybe I'm in a bad mood lately, or maybe my standards have suddently become impossibly high, but I didn't like this novel.<br/><br/><b>Brief recap of what this story is about</b>: to be with girl, boy has to acquire a soul. To do so, boy must pass an unspecified test. Girl has to do absolutely nothing in the meantime.<br/><br/>For the first 2/3 I was so bored that I wanted to gouge my eyes off with a</span>
  <span id="freeText566319364711956854" style="display:none">First, let me say that I really enjoyed the previous installments of this series; so I'm not happy to squash this one down. Maybe I'm in a bad mood lately, or maybe my standards have suddently become impossibly high, but I didn't like this novel.<br><br><b>Brief recap of what this story is about</b>: to be with girl, boy has to acquire a soul. To do so, boy must pass an unspecified test. Girl has to do absolutely nothing in the meantime.<br><br>For the first 2/3 I was so bored that I wanted to gouge my eyes off with a spoon.<br>The book is written in first person, from Ash's POV. Given that now he's kind of depressed, sad, tired, indecisive and generally behaves like an emo, that's not conductive for a lively read.<br><br>If you don't know what an "emo" is:<br><br><a href="http://www.nupxl.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/10/Demotivational_Poster__Emo_by_couhby1.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356074i/707852._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And then he discovers that his ex girlfriend is not dead, but is still pining for him. She's almost as depressed and sad and all-of-the-above as he is.<br>What a huge pile of depression and sadness. Shall we throw an emo party? (Or is that an oxymoron?)<br>From that point on, I trudged on just to see her die. Because it was obvious that sooner or later she would, possibly in a coherently sad and depressing way.<br>(Here I was thinking "<i>if I'm lucky, she's going to cut herself or something</i>")<br><br>Well, our depressed and sad characters face a series of pointless and wholly inconsequential challenges. I'm sure there's every sort of metaphorical significance in those, but all the philosophizing is lost on me. I just found these parts unnecessary. Maybe they were needed to give some thickness to the book.<br><br>And then Ash comes to the End of the World where he'll prove himself worthy of a soul. We are on chapter 15 out of 24, and you could delete all that's already happened without losing anyhing of the plot's backbone (as detailed in my nice recap).<br><br>The trial consists in three rather stupid tests. Sorry, but I'll have to need some spoilers here.<br>- The first test is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[survive a pretended attack of monstrous birds without using glamour (fey magic) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>; and no one has ever done that before!? Please.<br>- The second test is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[to relive all the bad actions he has committed <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>; same comment as above.<br>- The third test is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[to grow old, while your immortal companion never ages <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. As this require some insight in the future, it can be confused with the normal course of events. For me, this part was a continuous string of WTFs.<br><br>Finally, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[we are freed from the burdensome presence of the ex girlfriend, who kindly sacrifices herself for the happiness of her boyfriend with his new girlfriend.<br><b>...WHAT!?</b><br>So, our boy can live happily-ever-after with the new girlfriend, carrying around the soul of his ex. Because it's not like this is creepy or bothersome in the least. In fact, I'd love to know my boyfriend lives with the soul of his ex. Absolutely <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br>Bottom line: don't bother with the actual book, just hit all the spoilers above and call it a day.<br>In the meantime, I'm going to pull a certain author down from a very high pedestal.<br><br><br><br>DISCLAIMER:<br>This review is meant as a joke. I don't intend to belittle depression or other kinds of psychological distress. I've suffered of depression myself, so believe me, I should know.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="566319364711956854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_129813694" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who loves to be told an EPIC story!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3239811-michele-reading-lark-canadiantwimom?shelf=fey-faeries">fey-faeries</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129813694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16852510911564371199"><br/>Simply put... PURE PERFECTION! <br/> <br/>Story telling does not get any better than this... <br/> <br/>I am utterly struggling for the right words to adequately review the brilliance of The Iron Knight, and the series as a whole, and do it ANY justice, so please bear with me. <br/> <br/>How could Julie Kagawa meet the excellent story telling of The Iron Queen and her previous books in her series? While, from past experience, I had no doubt she could... I was still amazed that SHE DID... so expertly and so eloquently as only</span>
  <span id="freeText16852510911564371199" style="display:none"><br />Simply put... PURE PERFECTION! <br /> <br />Story telling does not get any better than this... <br /> <br />I am utterly struggling for the right words to adequately review the brilliance of The Iron Knight, and the series as a whole, and do it ANY justice, so please bear with me. <br /> <br />How could Julie Kagawa meet the excellent story telling of The Iron Queen and her previous books in her series? While, from past experience, I had no doubt she could... I was still amazed that SHE DID... so expertly and so eloquently as only a master story teller can do.<br /><br />Going into this final installment in The Iron Fey, we knew that this was going to be Ash's story and it would be about his journey in finding his way back to Meghan. Meghan is now the Queen of the Iron realm -- a place where Ash, as a faery, cannot follow despite his vow to protect her as her knight. Ash's solution to be with her again is to become human... he admits to not fully understandng what it will require of him, but he's determined to do whatever it takes to keep his promise to her.<br /> <br />As much as this was a story about Ash's pursuit of becoming human and ultimately returning to Meghan's side, it also became a very personal journey for him as well. Not only does he have to meet some very hard challenges head-on that involve strength, determination and skill, he also had to make some excrutiating choices, too. Is his love for Meghan strong enough to get him through this - that is also put to the test. The tests are next to impossible... no other has lived to tell about it. <br /> <br />Ash's evolution from The Iron King to this last installment in The Iron Fey series is, in my opinion, one of the best character arcs I've ever read... and probably more so than Meghan's, which I thought was very impressive. We thought we finally broke through Ash's icey-facade in The Iron Queen, but what we find in The Iron Knight, is that there is many more layers that needed peeling away to get to the heart of this amazing character. And some of what we find at his core is not pretty, and difficult to reconcile with the Ash we all have loved in these books. Julie took a huge risk in humbling the icey-prince but it was so well done and purposeful.<br /> <br />Ash's arduous and yet fantastical journey takes us to the edges of the Nevernever... to The River of Dreams and The Deep Wylde, and culminates at The End of the World and The Testing Grounds, all the while accompanied by Puck and Grimalkin and two VERY unlikely characters from Ash's past.<br /> <br />During Ash's quest, Julie cleverly inserted some wonderfully romantic moments as well (remember... this is Ash's quest to <i>returning</i> to Meghan's side). And Julie knows how to write about love without it being corny or mushy... just natural, heart-melting and sigh-worthy.<br /> <br />Puck also plays a pivotal role in Ash's journey - he does not just provide the comic relief and live to be the thorn in Ash's side. I have to say that he really shines in The Iron Knight. While I've always loved his lightheartedness and funny antics... we get to see a lot more of the REAL Puck, and I loved him for it. Some of the best scenes were between him and Ash. I really came to ADORE and appreciate Puck in this final book.<br /> <br />Of course, Grimalkin is... well... Grimalkin. As always, he pops in when it's convenient for him and mysteriously vanishes when trouble is near. He never changes, there is no personal growth, but he plays one of the most enjoyable parts in this series.<br /> <br />There were two surprising characters who join Ash in his quest and they were wonderful additions to the story and so very integral. I can't provide more description than that without providing some big spoilers, so you'll have to take my word for it till you can read for yourself.<br /> <br />The Iron Knight reached beyond my expectations and Ash gave a whole new meaning to that old declaration of love, "I'll go to the ends of the earth for you." I couldn't ask for a more befitting ending either, where we briefly switch back to Meghan's perspective. And that very last page just hit it out of the park for me. Julie nailed it with that very last scene. It was understated just a bit... but so very perfect.<br /> <br />So now my all-time favourite story has come to an end and I'm left with a mish-mash of incredibly content and sad emotions. Throughout The Iron Fey series, Julie took us to some very magical, fantastical, almost impossible to imagine places... all through some pretty wonderful story telling. <br /> <br />Thank you to Netgalley and Harlequin Teen for the privilege of reading this early. Now I won't have to wish the summer away afterall. Meghan, Ash, Puck, Grimalkin and a wonderful cast of supporting characters will forever live in my heart and never cease to exist. Most of all... thank you Julie for sharing your brilliant imagination with us.<br /><br />Originally read: July 16-23, 2011<br /><br />Audio: I listened to the audio of The Iron Knight over the last couple of weeks. I LOVED reliving Ash's journey to gaining his soul and finding his way back to Meghan. What an adventure! The narrator's voice was smooth, albeit, somewhat older sounding for Ash a bit too New Yorkish (??) for Puck, but awesome for Grim, and the female voice imitations were a little funny coming from such a masculine voice...but I did get used to him and quite enjoyed his narration. I also appreciated the Meghan's voice returning at the end for the epilogue...perfect!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16852510911564371199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer273494044169265580"><b>Final rating: 2/5 stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376685ra/731691.gif' width='400' height='175' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>This will be a really difficult review to write...this is my fifth time of rewriting it actually. </b><br/><br/>I enjoyed the book, and i loved the story. It's a roller coaster of emotions (as a matter of fact, i cried, laughed like crazy and was pissed off and raging a lot).<br/><br/> But! But! And more but! there is a reason it's not higher than 2. The reason lies in our famous ice prince of the Winter court, Ash.<br/><b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731693.jpg' width='400' height='250' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>There is just one thing for certain. You will either hate or still love Ash - or b</b></span>
  <span id="freeText273494044169265580" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 2/5 stars</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376685ra/731691.gif" width="400" height="175" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This will be a really difficult review to write...this is my fifth time of rewriting it actually. </b><br><br>I enjoyed the book, and i loved the story. It's a roller coaster of emotions (as a matter of fact, i cried, laughed like crazy and was pissed off and raging a lot).<br><br> But! But! And more but! there is a reason it's not higher than 2. The reason lies in our famous ice prince of the Winter court, Ash.<br><b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731693.jpg" width="400" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There is just one thing for certain. You will either hate or still love Ash - or be stuck in between like me. And that decision can be, or... most possibly... life destroying.</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, the thing is that this book was kind of weird to me. Weird as in dinosaur in middle of a town, playing with children. Oh wait, i don't need to imagine it, here it is:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376685ra/731695.gif" width="400" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And still i cannot say that i didn't love this book. Because i did. It was addicting and i couldn't stop reading it even if i wanted.</b> I wanted to know what happened next, and next and next. I also liked the story, even if it was cliched in some parts but i loooooooooooooved it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b><br>I never thought i would actually miss being in Meghan's head, because i really <i>did</i> miss her. Being in Ash's head was tiring sometimes.<br><br>It's true! O_O</b><br><br><blockquote> <b>► STORY</b>: </blockquote><br><br>After the end of third book, where Meghan claimed her throne and became the Iron Queen, she exiled Ash using his true name to keep him away from staying with her and dying in pain. <br><br>So, our stubborn fey prince swears an oath to find a way to be with her again. <br><br>Which leads him to being in a company of his frenemy Puck, Grimalkin, Big Bad Wolf and......<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ariella <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Le gasp!<br><br>Which makes him question... does he truly love Meghan and will he be able to do everything to be with her?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> BE WARNED: SPOILERRRRRRRRRRRRRRRS. SERIOUS ONE IN FACT, AS IN END OF THE BOOK SPOILERS</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>Those trials were freaking awesome O_O!!!! I loved how they made Ash suffer, mwahahahaha. He did deserve it, but i kind of felt sad in the end... Especially with all of his regrets. At least he regretted the monstrosities he did. But the final one, with vision of the future... it kind of broke my heart :(<br><br>Then, the visions. They were kind of.... interesting. Especially Ash being the winter king and killing everyone O.o... But Puck died so i was not happy about it.<br><br>And chapter 14 with mirror reflections - epic! I loved that chapter the most &lt;3<br><br>and i cried during the part where Ash and Puck fought for the last time :(<br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br><blockquote> <b>► CHARACTERS</b>: </blockquote><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Ash</u>
  </i>
</b>:<br><br>Ash fans, please don't kill me.<br><br>#cause i have an opinion. <br><br>Ash, the winter prince, the one who makes the whole world swoon - drastically changes in this book. I don't know what happened, but this is not Ash i was used to. It is different, whiny, undecidable character. As much as i loved him before, my opinion drastically changed as much as it did with him.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I was in love. With a human.<br>I smiled bitterly at the thought. The old Ash, if faced with such a suggestion, would've either laughed scornfully or removed the offender's head from his neck. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>As far as i know, i am able to tolerate irritating heroes and heroines. And i once loved Ash. Now, i want him to burn in hell (actually i want him to suffer, because what he had gone through was really not nearly enough for what he had done in the past). Well, not really, i don't. But i do. And then again, i don't. I am quite conflicted about my feelings for him.<br><br>I just know that i want my old Ash back. This version of him destroyed everything i loved about him. If i could just go back in time or erase everything which irritated me (which would be from chapter 6 to chapter 14)....sigh....it would be awesome :D<br><br><b>Serious spoilers:</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>As for his past, as mentioned above... i can understand that he was not, in fact, always a positive character. He did belong to the evil side of the faeries, to the emotionless, brutal and uncaring race. And what he did before was unspeakable and nothing can change it. No matter how much he regretted it, it wasn't enough. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Are you sure you want to proceed? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Nothing can change that he was in fact, a cold blooded murderer, kind of rapist, destroyer of lives and stealer of babies. Nope, he lost my respect for that.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br>So, the appearance of Ariella was kind of irritating to me. Because, all Ash did was think if he loved Meghan or Ariella more. It pissed me off so much. And i couldn't bear it and it made me rage over and over again. I get it that he loved her once, and that he was truly in love with her, but its time to let the past go, and embrace the present. He loves Meghan too, but after this book, i was not convinced. It felt like he was doing it only for himself, because if he hadn't sworn an oath, he would probably be with Ariella. But he had to do it, and therefore he had to be with Meghan because he couldn't do anything else. And that made me hate him in a way. And when he did get his soul, he stayed with Meghan ONLY because of a vision of his son. Again, he did not do it for Meghan. and yet again he said this:<br><br><blockquote><i><b> “Ari...I will always love you. I always have.Nothing will change that." I squeezed her hand, then gently released it. "You'll always be a part of me. But...I'm not in love with you...anymore.And despite my promise,despite seeing you again, I do this because I want to be with Meghan, nothing else" Ariella's eyes glazed over, and I eased back, speaking as gently as I could "I can't be yours, Ariella. I'm sorry.” </b></i></blockquote>
<br><br>And everything he endured in the trials was well deserved. But i think he should have suffered more.<br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And yet, i still kind of love him. But not as much as i did before, and in the end, i was sad for him. After all, he was one of my favorite characters before. Many people forgave him, but i just cant decide.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Puck</u>
  </i>
</b>:<br><br>I totally root for him now. I love him, and have always loved him, ever since the first book. Despite everything, he was always there. No matter how much it hurt him or damaged him, he was always there to support. I actually love him the most, and i think it would have been better if Meghan actually stayed with him instead of Ash. He truly loves her. I even think he was more and better characterized than any other character in the series. I even cried for him! After all he didn't lose one, but three people he loved the most. Two friends and the love of his life.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> "Just because we have a different way of handling it, doesn’t mean I don’t have scars of my own.”<br>“Name one,” I scoffed. “Give me one instance where you haven’t—”<br>“Meghan Chase!” Puck roared, startling me into silence. I blinked, and he sneered at me. “Yeah, your highness. I know what loss is. I’ve loved that girl since before she knew me. But I waited. I waited because I didn’t want to lie about who I was. I wanted her to know the truth before anything else. So I waited, and I did my job. For years, I protected her, biding my time, until the day she went into the Nevernever after her brother. And then you came along. And I saw how she looked at you. And for the first time, I wanted to kill you as much as you wanted to kill me."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Everyone else</u>
  </i>
</b>:<br><br>◉<b> Grimalkin </b>was as awesome as usual, i think he was even more cooler in this one of them all. And he is always, oh so mysterious. <br>◉ The character who returned from the Winter's passage is the<b> Big Bad Wolf</b>, and he was a nice addition and his arguments with Grimalkin were so hilarious!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “The Wolf snarled, tensing his muscles, as if he wished he could climb the tree after the feline. "One day I will catch you on the ground, cat," he said through bared teeth. "And you won't even know I'm there until I tear your head off." "You have been saying that since before humans had fire, dog," Grimalkin replied, completely undisturbed. "You'll have to forgive me if I don't hold my breath." </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>◉The mystery guest of this book: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <b>Ariella!</b>...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I kind of feel sad about her. She did survive and everything but was forced to see everything that happened to Ash and Puck and Meghan.... But i didn't want her here and i just wanted her to go away as soon as possible. It is clear how much Ash loved her - and it made me dislike her.<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>◉ <b>Meghan</b> did not appear much in this one, but i think i love her even more now.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote> <b>► OVERALL</b>: </blockquote><br><br>Don't get me wrong - i looooooooooooooove this series. And it's worth reading. But, i kind of prefer how third book ended comparing to this end. But still, interesting addition and i need more of these books. Thank god there are more ;D<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And p.s. Because of this i did not do anything productive for past two days.<br><br>Except writing this enormous review.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And p.s. the end of the book dialogues were so much fun &lt;3<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Puck: Well, she likes me best, of course. I’m the handsome, charming one.<br>Ash: Yes, that’s why she gave you your own book. Oh, wait.<br>Puck: No one asked you, ice-boy.<br>Julie: I like them all in different ways. But I will say that Ash was the hardest character to write sometimes. It’s so hard to get him to talk! I’ll be pushing him to open up and say something and he just crosses his arms and acts stubborn.<br>Ash: …<br>Julie: See?<br></b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> Tell us a little about other things that interest you, besides writing.<br>Julie: Well, I enjoy reading, painting and drawing, but I also love anime, manga and comics. I’m an avid gamer—I have a PS3, an Xbox 360 and a Wii. My favorite food in the whole world is sushi, and I’m taking classes in Wing Tzun kung fu.<br>Puck: *singing* “Everybody was kung fu fighting …”<br>Julie: Agh. Ash, stop him before that song is stuck in everyone’s head.<br>Ash: Too late.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>What is your favorite part of the Nevernever? Where would you live if you were a faery?<br>Julie: I was going to say the wyldwood, but on second thought, I think I’d live in the Iron Realm with Meghan and Ash.<br>Ash: See? She prefers my company to yours.<br>Julie: Not really. It’s just hard to find a wireless signal in the wyldwood.<br>Puck: *snicker*</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731692.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>

<div id="review_129827780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129827780" />
    <a title="Sandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy"><img alt="Sandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320017147p2/4515165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129827780?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy">Sandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=chemistry-sigh">chemistry-sigh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=endings-i-love">endings-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=can-t-stop-thinking-about">can-t-stop-thinking-about</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=premise-i-love">premise-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=favorite-character">favorite-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=settings-i-love">settings-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=whiplash-twists">whiplash-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129827780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2950836406108199792"><b>Julie Kagawa knows how to end a series.</b><br/><br/>It's always sad (and a bit scary) to say goodbye to a favorite series. Last books come with such emotionally-fueled expectations. And after, some authors leave you feeling wrung out and crushed, while other authors make your heart sigh with happiness and contentment. Whenever I read a last book, I'm always overwhelmed with that feeling of <i>Please don't ruin what you've created.</i> Well, I am ecstatic to say that in <i>The Iron Knight</i>, Julie Kagawa gives us the per</span>
  <span id="freeText2950836406108199792" style="display:none"><b>Julie Kagawa knows how to end a series.</b><br /><br />It's always sad (and a bit scary) to say goodbye to a favorite series. Last books come with such emotionally-fueled expectations. And after, some authors leave you feeling wrung out and crushed, while other authors make your heart sigh with happiness and contentment. Whenever I read a last book, I'm always overwhelmed with that feeling of <i>Please don't ruin what you've created.</i> Well, I am ecstatic to say that in <i>The Iron Knight</i>, Julie Kagawa gives us the perfect journey to the perfect ending that this stellar series deserves.<br /><br /><i>The Iron Knight</i> was one of my most highly anticipated books of 2011, and WOW did Julie deliver. It was everything I was hoping for: adventure, anguish, romance, danger, and a slew of game-changing twists that left my head spinning. Within the first ten pages, Julie hit me with a whiplash twist that I just didn't see coming (the summary wasn't available then) and then she kept them coming for the rest of the story. Things that weren't anywhere on my radar were thrown into the mix, keeping the story fresh and compelling.<br /><br />And let's talk about ASH. This is his story. His narration is everything my little fangirl heart was wishing for: some moments were pure bliss, and others, as Ash begins to thaw that icy cold heart, were harrowing and heart-wrenching. Everything about Ash--his emotions, his intense love, his regret--is laid bare. We see every vulnerability Ash hides behind that cold exterior, and we feel the extent of his absolute devotion to Meghan. And as Ash has told Meghan many times, there are horrific crimes in his past, and as Ash atones for those crimes to be worthy of what it will take to be with Meghan, we see how much his love for her has changed him--how much her love for him as already redeemed him.<br /><br />For fans worried there may not be enough Meghan, I thought Julie devised some sneaky, delicious ways to fit in plenty of Meghan. Besides, we've had three books with her, and I'm a sucker for any kind of alternate POV, especially from the hero's perspective, to truly feel the extent of his love for our heroine.<br /><br />So this Ash fangirl thanks you, Julie Kagawa, for creating such a satisfying, stirring end to this beloved series. I found myself re-reading entire chapters just so I didn't have to say goodbye so soon.<br /><br /><br />(And let's all give Julie's editor a big cheer for convincing Julie to write <i>The Iron Knight</i> and not leave that heartbreaking goodbye in <i>The Iron Queen</i> as the end like Julie initially intended. Yes, those parting words of Ash and Meghan in TIQ were tragic and all-sacrificing and made me cry, but oh, how I love my happily ever after instead.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2950836406108199792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2328379894" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2328379894" />
    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2328379894?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=paranormal-read">paranormal-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2328379894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3589901625994370067">Since I haven’t written reviews for the first 3 books I would like to start off by saying that all four of the books get 4.5 stars from me. I was pleasantly startled to see that it was really easy to get absorbed into this world and I got through each book pretty quickly. When I started this series, I think the first thing I noticed was that the plot for each book is relatively simple and the figuring out the twists and turns was not a hardship at all. Despite the simplicity of the storyline, I </span>
  <span id="freeText3589901625994370067" style="display:none">Since I haven’t written reviews for the first 3 books I would like to start off by saying that all four of the books get 4.5 stars from me. I was pleasantly startled to see that it was really easy to get absorbed into this world and I got through each book pretty quickly. When I started this series, I think the first thing I noticed was that the plot for each book is relatively simple and the figuring out the twists and turns was not a hardship at all. Despite the simplicity of the storyline, I was shocked to see that books somehow always managed to keep me wanting to read more. <br /><br />The books were overall very entertaining and in due course of time, grow on you. The ‘fairy’ world of Nevernever comprises of the Seelie Court, the Unseelie Court, and now the Iron Kingdom. I enjoyed seeing the incorporation of the characters from <i>A Midsummer Night’s Dream</i> as humans began dreaming of them. The idea that myths, stories, and simply remembering a creature from a story fuels their existence in the book. <br /><br />Our protagonist, Meghan, is not one of my favorite female leads but there is a vast growth in her character when compared with her personality in the first book. In the first 2 books I feel like she has a hard time keeping her emotions from overriding her actions so they lead to situations that could have been better or even completely avoided, but in the third book she is more put together and makes well thought out decisions and comes into her own. I truly admire her loyalty to the people who matter to her and her willingness to do what is right even if it is very much easier to extricate herself from the issue.  <br /><br />I also really love both Ash and Puck, both of them have great personalities and are the most loyal friends you will find. Those last chapters revealed a lot about both Ash and Puck not just to us but themselves. Puck's fame and other people's opinions and previous encounters with him are truly amusing. Reading about bits of their past as best friends is so endearing it make my heart want of shatter into a million pieces.<br />And you can't not love Grimalkin.<br /><br />I don’t think the entirety of how attached I’d become to this world, to these characters hit me only when I was reading this final book. As I neared the end of this book the reality that I was actually going to leave this world of faeries, love, and friendship hit me like a punch to the gut. Each of the character in their own way have grown on me to the point that I will always want to come back to these characters, I will truly miss this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3589901625994370067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1530336610" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1530336610" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1530336610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4610413145249752899"><b>2.5</b> for the same reason <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1530242812?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Iron Queen</a> is a 2.5. Some parts are just so tedious and useless.<br/><br/><b>"I will be with her again, or I will die."</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394149950ra/8814372.gif' width='420' height='240' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>(this gif is everything)<br/><br/>Yeah, I know that there was all that oath thing, so he was obliged to keep his word, yadda yadda, but stil: <i>gag</i>.<br/><br/>•I<b> did</b> like<b> Ash </b>as main character more than Meghan; not that it took that much, considering that when I began to read <i>The Iron Knight</i> I could formulate just one intelligible thought, and it was: No more Meghan for a while. Yes. <b>Ye</b></span>
  <span id="freeText4610413145249752899" style="display:none"><b>2.5</b> for the same reason <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1530242812?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Queen</a> is a 2.5. Some parts are just so tedious and useless.<br><br><b>"I will be with her again, or I will die."</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394149950ra/8814372.gif" width="420" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(this gif is everything)<br><br>Yeah, I know that there was all that oath thing, so he was obliged to keep his word, yadda yadda, but stil: <i>gag</i>.<br><br>•I<b> did</b> like<b> Ash </b>as main character more than Meghan; not that it took that much, considering that when I began to read <i>The Iron Knight</i> I could formulate just one intelligible thought, and it was: No more Meghan for a while. Yes. <b>Yes</b>. <br>(For further information, see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1428282195" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron King</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1528622194" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Daughter</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1530242812" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Queen</a> and call Meghan all the names under the sun along with me.)<br>So, as I said, Ash was not that terrible. But then <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>Ariella</b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> joined the gang, because apparently Kagawa is completely incapable of writing a book without trotting out a <b>love-triangle</b>. As if this were not enough, the explanation given for her return is totally <b>plucked out of thin air</b>, just because the author thinks that without all this useless, nauseating and gratuitous <b>drama</b> a story cannot be interesting, quite apart from the fact that she herself is contradictory in trying to give clarifications as to what actually happened: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[first it is said the she is actually alive (even if more than once it is implied that she may be something more akin to a ghost or something similar), and indeed at last she gives her life in order for Ash to gain his soul. But then Grimalkin says this:<br><br><b>"She was already dead, prince.” Grimalkin paused and looked back at me, narrowing his eyes. “She perished the day you swore your oath against Goodfellow."</b><br><br>But then she couldn't have actually given her life and I've wasted my time reading shit!<br><br>Oh, screw it, I'm done with this nonsense. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>To me, this is called <b>ineffective and clumsy usage of narrative devices</b>.<br><br>•What pushed me to give half a star more were the chapters in which Ash faces his <b>three trials</b>, which are the only parts of the book I found truly and completely interesting and that didn't annoy or bored me at all, except for the third trial, which in my opinion takes up too many space and could have been rewritten in a more effective way. My favorite is without doubt the second trial, when finally we get to see what a bastard Ash was in the first centuries of his life. It reminded me why I started this series in the first place, to see Faeries being<b> mean, sly, sneaky and cunning</b>. Which, sadly for me, I didn't. Not at all. <br>Had I known...<br><br>•The <b>banter</b> between Ash and Puck was funny to follow at times, just flat at others. And some of Puck's jokes are really off-putting. Sometimes I didn't know whether to laugh or cry.<br><br>•Half of the <b>plot</b> is filled with random attacks from monsters and co. that have no connection with Ash's quest and whose only purpose is to fill with <i>something</i> a hundred pages more, thus my boredom and my luck of interest.<br><br>In a nutshell, what I recommend you is to steer clear of this series. <u>
  <b>My overall rating considering the four books as a whole is 2.5 stars out of 5</b>
</u>, so it's not utterly terrible, but reading these books was an agony for me. Besides, as I said, even without considering my personal feeling towards the characters and their attitudes, the series lacks of a solid structure and presents various logical inconsistencies. I can find very little of good in it, maybe only the main concept, which had, in my opinion, a lot of potential.<br><br>And I am sad for this, because, seriously, you have no idea how much I wanted to love <i>The Iron Fey</i>. It just wasn't meant to be.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4610413145249752899" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_229364176" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229364176" />
    <a title="Soumi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6833452-soumi"><img alt="Soumi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440767658p2/6833452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229364176?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Soumi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Soumi" href="/user/show/6833452-soumi">Soumi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=books-i-reviewed">books-i-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=fairies">fairies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229364176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1847877569444340764"><b>From this day forth, I vow to protect Meghan Chase, daughter of the Summer King, with my sword, my honor and my life. Should even the world stand against her, my blade will be at her side. And should it fail to protect her, let my own life be forfeit.</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362197i/713355._SX540_.png' width='600' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I must say I have taken a brave attempt to write the review of The Iron Knight when I’m out of my words how to praise this book. How can I describe how much I loved this book when I’m still lost in thoughts and my hands are numb and shaking to write</span>
  <span id="freeText1847877569444340764" style="display:none"><b>From this day forth, I vow to protect Meghan Chase, daughter of the Summer King, with my sword, my honor and my life. Should even the world stand against her, my blade will be at her side. And should it fail to protect her, let my own life be forfeit.</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362197i/713355._SX540_.png" width="600" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I must say I have taken a brave attempt to write the review of The Iron Knight when I’m out of my words how to praise this book. How can I describe how much I loved this book when I’m still lost in thoughts and my hands are numb and shaking to write this review? The Iron Knight is an EPIC romance of this decade, I doubt I will ever be able to love any other book like I loved this one, its characters. <br>The last three book of this series was form point of view of Meghan Chase, this one is narrated by Ashallayn’darkmyr Tallyn, our very own Prince Ash, his quest to find a way to be mortal and be with his Iron Queen Meghan. In his journey he was accompanied by his old rival summer court prankster Robin “Puck” Goodfellow, Grimalkin the wise cat, the big bad Wolf, and his lost love Ariella who were assumed dead in previous books.<br>No book has ever made me cry like The Iron Knight. I cried when Ash attempted to end Puck life suppressed by ever burning rage of lost and pain, Puck stood still gazing directly into Ash with his bright green eyes confessing his love for Meghan, his pain, his loss, I cried when Ariella helped them in their quest sacrificing her love and life for Ash. <br>I felt empty when I finished this book, I felt something has gone from my life, something has ended.<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2995873.Julie_Kagawa" title="Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie Kagawa</a> did a fantastic job, what a captivating, mesmerizing writing. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2995873.Julie_Kagawa" title="Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie Kagawa</a> knows how to bring our imagination into pages, she took us into a memorable journey, showed us an unseen fey world. I felt myself as a part this team marching forward through the fairy territory to the end of the world in order fulfill the quest.<br><br><i>
  <b>Knight In Shinning Armor</b>
</i><br><br><b>I have come from the End of the World.... From the River of Dreams, through the gauntlet and the Briar and the Deep Wyld, in order to stand before you today. I have but one request - to take my place at your side. To resume my duty as your knight, and to protect you and your kingdom for as long as I draw breath.</b><br>Ashallayn’darkmyr Tallyn you are the best male protagonist I have ever came through. He is the true knight, who doesn’t know how to step back from keeping his oath, made impossible into possible for his love. He is the dream guy of any girl. As we knew Ash has an icy cold barrier surrounding his heart which beats for Meghan, the only girl whose touch has melted the ice away. But in this book we also felt the warmth of his heart too, haunted by guilt, torn between past and present, we felt his nightmares, his pain, his love and fierce devotion for the one girl, we saw the true Ash who sometime can be vulnerable. He didn’t hesitate once to sacrifice everything he has. Ash and Meghan went through a lot to be with each other and they deserve a happy ending, I’m just glad that Ash finally found his way to his love.<br><br><i>
  <b>The Summer Prankster</b>
</i><br><br><b>So I waited, and I did my job. For years, I protected her, biding my time, until the day she went into the Nevernever after her brother. And then you came along. And I saw how she looked at you. And for the first time, I wanted to kill you as much as you wanted to kill me.</b><br>Puck is as always dynamic, brought smile into my lips throughout the whole book. In spite of his all attempts to hide his emotional distress I felt his pain of losing the one and only girl he has ever loved to the person he shared a cold enmity for centuries. Puck taught me love doesn’t mean to be with the person, love means to make that person happy, even if it costs sacrificing your feelings. I may adore Ash but I’m a more Puck girl. I tried hard to refrain my tears each and every time I realized how much torture it is for Puck to wear a mask of fake smile while his is heart is burning in pain. He never showed how much he felt guilty for bearing the death of Ariella on his conscience, we realized his grief of losing Arilla and his pain of losing his best friend. He fought off every obstacle, every danger shoulder in shoulder with Ash, without Puck, the story is incomplete.<br><br><i>
  <b>Turning Point</b>
</i><br><br>Bringing Ariella back was the most surprising element of the story, she just made a big place in my heart. I sucked my breath, tried hard to hold back my tears to watch her to sacrifice herself so that Ash can be with his love. She loved Ash soooo much, still she never let her love came into his way. That’s what I call true love. <br>How can I forget cute Grim, Awwwww, I love you. Without you Ash and Puck would be lost, You are the most wise, witty guide and loyal friend. <br>I truly doubt without Puck and Ariella, Grim and the Wolf, Ash would ever be able to find his way back to Meghan.<br>This book is a heart wrenching romantic fantasy novel, it took my breath away. <br>Thank you very much <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2995873.Julie_Kagawa" title="Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie Kagawa</a> for such a wonderful gift. This whole series will remain forever in core of my heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1847877569444340764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
