<div id="review_130222534" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130222534" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130222534?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=cover-crazz">cover-crazz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=fey-folk">fey-folk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=own-copy">own-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130222534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12822389470090016479">Have you ever wanted to read a book so badly, and wanting it to be everything you hoped it would be, and then it turn out to met not only your expectations but went beyond anything you could imagine? <br/>Well, that what's happened to me after reading <b>The Iron Knight.</b><br/><br/>I feel in love with this series right from the very first book. One after the other getting stronger and better. So when I heard the last and final book was on it's way I was excited to see how it would end and sad to see this beloved wo</span>
  <span id="freeText12822389470090016479" style="display:none">Have you ever wanted to read a book so badly, and wanting it to be everything you hoped it would be, and then it turn out to met not only your expectations but went beyond anything you could imagine? <br />Well, that what's happened to me after reading <b>The Iron Knight.</b><br /><br />I feel in love with this series right from the very first book. One after the other getting stronger and better. So when I heard the last and final book was on it's way I was excited to see how it would end and sad to see this beloved world and it's characters go, but after reading the final book I was filled with such contentment and a satisfaction that rarely happens with books. See I always, <i>always</i> want more, but the way Julie Kagawa wraps this up is pure perfection. <br /><br />I don't know how Kagawa does it really, but I'm always floored, amazed and in complete awe of this women imagination and creativity. Really, how does she come up with this stuff? Her writing is like word-candy that I want to devour and savor at the exact same time. The world is so vivid, busting with energetic characters and adventure so colorful and fantastical that I want to climb in the pages, hide in a tree and just witness it firsthand. The plots get thicker and richer with each book and just when I think that Julie can't outdo herself, she proves me wrong by throwing twists after remarkable twists, making her readers hang on every.single.word at the very edge of their seats. <br />Amazing, amazing stuff!<br /><br />In The Iron Knight, we follow Ash and Puck as they try to find a way for Ash to keep his vow to Meghan. Through an absolutely soaring journey across the River of Dreams, and to the depths of the End of the World, while fighting constant evil surrounding their every step. Trials must be faced, old feuds met and a past filled with regrets and sorrow put to rest. But fear not, for Ash and Puck are accompanied with a couple of familiar characters and one other companion that we <i>nevah</i> saw coming.<br /><br />This was by far my favorite of the <i>Iron Fey</i> books. Not only did I simply <i>adore</i> the ending, I also loved that we finally got a glimpse of Ash and his very complex thoughts. <br />We learn the story of Ash and Ariella and get to see Ash and Puck on civil terms (but not tongues mind you) I adore the teamwork. They seem like such an unlikely pair cause of their heated history, but it felt as natural as breathing with these two. <br />I laughed, I cried and I felt like a sentimental fool.<br />I was pretty shocked with what Ash was attempting to do, as well as the <i>incredible</i> twist I never even thought could happen, but I forgot I was in Julie's world and anything pretty much goes. But I think what I loved most was the challenges Ash had to face and how he dealt with each one. Illuminating the human spirit and recognizing it for what it's truly worth.<br /><br />I can go on forever praising this book but I think you get the picture. I loved it would never be enough. So all I'm gonna say is that for any fans of this epic series, this book is a must have to add to your collection.<br />I will miss Ash and Meghan, Puck and Grim and the countless adventures, but while their story ends here, another will begin in her Iron Fey Spinoff that stars Meghan's brother, Ethan, all grown up. It is greatly anticipated as well as anything else Julie writes. Her books are all a must-have in my eyes.<br /><br />Congrats to Julie Kagawa on the success of this exceptional series. <br />It will forever be treasured among my favorites!<br /><br />Team Ash &lt;3!!!!<br /><br />(Special thanks to Netgalley and Harlequin teen)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12822389470090016479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_142096922" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142096922" />
    <a title="Diane ϟ [ Lestrange ]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3442094-diane-lestrange"><img alt="Diane ϟ [ Lestrange ]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365914493p2/3442094.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142096922?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane ϟ [ Lestrange ]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane ϟ [ Lestrange ]" href="/user/show/3442094-diane-lestrange">Diane ϟ [ Lestrange ]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3442094-diane-lestrange?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3442094-diane-lestrange?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3442094-diane-lestrange?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3442094-diane-lestrange?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3442094-diane-lestrange?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3442094-diane-lestrange?shelf=surely-i-ll-never-forget-book">surely-i-ll-never-forget-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3442094-diane-lestrange?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142096922" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4212335444670282937"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380344364i/699366.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I’m very thankful that Julie Kagawa didn’t leave us the bittersweet ending of Megan and Ash story in the 3rd book (The Iron Queen) for making this 4th . . . <i>[drum roll]</i> <b>The Iron Knight</b>!<br/><br/>As the final installment of Iron fey series, Ash must take an impossible journey to find his way back to Megan. Since as Winter Fey he cannot survive in the Iron Kingdom and being a human is his only choice but will it be that easy to be human or more gaining a soul? Does he understand what that solution really me</span>
  <span id="freeText4212335444670282937" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380344364i/699366.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’m very thankful that Julie Kagawa didn’t leave us the bittersweet ending of Megan and Ash story in the 3rd book (The Iron Queen) for making this 4th . . . <i>[drum roll]</i> <b>The Iron Knight</b>!<br><br>As the final installment of Iron fey series, Ash must take an impossible journey to find his way back to Megan. Since as Winter Fey he cannot survive in the Iron Kingdom and being a human is his only choice but will it be that easy to be human or more gaining a soul? Does he understand what that solution really means? Would he still want it if he did?<br><br>It’s sad to see the characters and their journey that true marked in our heart comes to an end. For an amazing series I can say that this final book is almost perfect to its pure brilliance. Why almost? Because ehem I’m team Puck and I didn’t see his happy ending, what do you expect? Hell! That’s bloody broke my heart. Anyway, except to that, The Iron Knight had everything I could have asked for, maybe more. <br><br>We see our Icy prince and his icy heart melted slowly from Iron King to Iron Daughter and we loved him more in the Iron Queen. But did you think that you already see all of him in those three books? Well, being said that this book is at our prince point of view we see a side of him that I don’t think many people had ever seen before. Being inside his head was so . . . different. He isn't very chatty unlike Puck, and at first his thoughts are kind of dull and focus only at his mission. Gratefully, Puck and Grim was there plus the two new members of the gang to distract him and break his icy mind and have a party with Hitler. <br>Ok let see. Former Icy Prince + Summer Jester + “unknown” + smart-mouth cat + an irascible DOG = <i>Dynamic</i>. Oh maybe “<b>syntax error</b>”? nah! LOL<br><br>So overall this book is a <b>feast</b>. It has twice the number of adventures, twice the humor and twice remarkable compared to the previous books. The places they been and the quest of their journey leaves me enchanted and trap to its overwhelming brilliant imagination of Julie Kagawa. Her characters emotion strikes a chord within me. Especially the strings between Ash and Puck, their friendship is indisputable despite the tons differences they have.<br>Oh how much I love this book. Never get me bored, emotionally satisfying, and an epic adventure. I would like to tell you more but I don’t want to spoil them so ill just shut my fat mouth. And recommend it to those who want a new perception of fairy tale for them. Julie Kagawa’s talent surely will not let you down. <u>I promise.</u><br><br><i>Big thanks to <b>netgalley</b> of letting me read this book in advance.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4212335444670282937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_207306864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207306864" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/207306864?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=the-fae-are-so-scary">the-fae-are-so-scary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=annoying-love-triangle">annoying-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=never-saw-it-coming">never-saw-it-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2011">reviewed-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207306864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10376373341742844249"><b>
  <i>My name, my full, True Name, is Ashallyn'darkmyr Tallyn, and I am the last son of the Unseelie Court.</i>
</b><br/><br/>I was not a big fan of the first two Iron Fey books, but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8685612.The_Iron_Queen__Iron_Fey___3_' title='The Iron Queen (Iron Fey, #3) by Julie Kagawa' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Iron Queen</a> completely stole my heart! Those of you who've read it know all about the beautiful romance, the fierce battle and the bittersweet ending that ensued. I suspect many of her fans were unhappy with the way Kagawa wrapped things up. In fact, some were probably even outraged, but not me – <b>I loved it</b>. That’s why I wasn’t too t</span>
  <span id="freeText10376373341742844249" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>My name, my full, True Name, is Ashallyn'darkmyr Tallyn, and I am the last son of the Unseelie Court.</i>
</b><br /><br />I was not a big fan of the first two Iron Fey books, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8685612.The_Iron_Queen__Iron_Fey___3_" title="The Iron Queen (Iron Fey, #3) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Queen</a> completely stole my heart! Those of you who've read it know all about the beautiful romance, the fierce battle and the bittersweet ending that ensued. I suspect many of her fans were unhappy with the way Kagawa wrapped things up. In fact, some were probably even outraged, but not me – <b>I loved it</b>. That’s why I wasn’t too thrilled about The Iron Knight to begin with. A fourth book, written from Prince Ash's point of view, could only mean a different ending for him and Meghan. I’m not sorry that I got to spend more time with Ash, Puck and especially Grimalkin, I just wish there was a way to make everything less <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[perfect <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> in the end. <br /><br />The Iron Knight is an adventure novel. Ash, Puck, Grimalkin and the Big Bad Wolf travel to the End of the World knowing that no one has ever come back alive. Reaching the end of the Nevernever means almost certain death for them all, but Ash swore an oath that compels him to move forward. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[That boy sure loves his oaths. How very dramatic. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Of course Robin Goodfellow has his reasons for following the Winter prince through the enchanted forest, as does Grimalkin, my personal favorite. <br /><br />I'm obviously not a huge fan of love triangles and I was very upset that Julie Kagawa felt the need to add another one to this story, no matter how well she resolved it in the end. I also had some minor issues with the quest itself. To be honest, I found it a little boring at times and more suitable for 14-year-old boys. BUT there were parts that were fabulous and compelling, and they evened things out a bit. <br /><br />Worldbuilding is the strong point of this book. This time, Kagawa removed her characters from the comfort of both Summer And Winter Courts and built for them a completely new and very creepy challenge called the Deep Wyld. If you thought Tir Na Nog was full of hidden dangers, wait till you read about a ferry sliding through the River of Dreams or, even worse, Phaed, a city where everyone seems to forget the purpose of their existence in just one night. <br /><br />It is impossible to write more about their quest without including spoilers for the previous book. Suffice it to say that I didn’t miss Meghan at all. <br />Despite my many problems with The Iron Knight, it was still extremely fun and I'm happy Kagawa decided to write it. I'm not so sure about the spin-off trilogy, though. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10376373341742844249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Although, to be fare, I must admit that the fey has never been a favorite fantasy topic for me, unlike vampires, who are my number one fantasy beings. <br/><br/>Despite being left unmoved by the Iron Fey series, Julie Kagawa's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1228896866?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blood of Eden series</a> is still one of my favorite young-</span>
  <span id="freeText12893450131202706770" style="display:none">DNF<br /><br />I just don't care about anything that happens here. <div id="review_145320755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="nico" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2488751-nico"><img alt="nico" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296631522p2/2488751.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145320755?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="nico" class="user" itemprop="url" name="nico" href="/user/show/2488751-nico">nico</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer145320755" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9112490542609463069">I can only hope that this will put my heart at ease. After the iron queen, my heart felt shattered. I hope beyond hope that this ends up being ash and puck, their journey to find grim and hopefully mend the frayed fabric that was ash and meghan.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6601035744963980792"><b> You know that feeling you get when you finish the last book in a beloved series? Like a good friend just moved away?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380372390ra/725679.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm going to have a MASSIVE book hangover from this series.</b><br/><br/><u>This review is full of spoilers (Don't read it if you haven't finished this book;))</u><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<b>The Iron Knight = An emotional roller coaster of epic proportions.</b> <br/><br/>One minute I was laughing at Puck's jokes, the next I was dying inside because I felt so sorry for Ash. <br/><br/>Puck and Ash are my favorite characters in this series.</span></span>
  <span id="freeText6601035744963980792" style="display:none"><b> You know that feeling you get when you finish the last book in a beloved series? Like a good friend just moved away?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380372390ra/725679.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm going to have a MASSIVE book hangover from this series.</b><br><br><u>This review is full of spoilers (Don't read it if you haven't finished this book;))</u><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>The Iron Knight = An emotional roller coaster of epic proportions.</b> <br><br>One minute I was laughing at Puck's jokes, the next I was dying inside because I felt so sorry for Ash. <br><br>Puck and Ash are my favorite characters in this series. I love, love, LOVE their best-friends-turned-enemies relationship. It developed perfectly throughout this book. It got to the part where I actually felt sad about the loss of their once good friendship. And then you get to watch them grow closer again in this book. SO PERFECT. &lt;3<br>(Now that I think of it, who needs Meghan? I ship Ash/Puck. Kidding.;))<br><br><blockquote>"If Puck was dead, my world would become as cold and lifeless as the darkest night in the Winter Court." - Ash<br>
</blockquote>
<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413274ra/813486.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In the beginning of the book, I was a bit pissed at Ash. What really bugged me was the whole I-love-you-Ariella,-if-I-hadn't-made-that-promise-to-Meghan-I-don't-know-what-I'd-do thing. That really bothered me, because after reading 3 books from Meghan's POV, I kind of felt like I <i> was </i> Meghan, and god was I jealous of stupid Ariella. (Sorry, Ari. I'm biased here.) <br>But luckily, Ash eventually figured out that he wasn't in love with her anymore, so that ended well. <br><br>After that the crying started. That's when I really began feeling sorry for Ash. And when I say I felt sorry for him, what I mean is that I wanted to pull him out of that horrible book where terrible things kept happening to him, and just hug him and give him some chocolate and tell him that everything would be ok. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413274ra/813487.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>And I just kept thinking "Ash, what are you doing, you can't become mortal! Meghan's immortal now, you can't start aging now! DON'T DO IT!"<br><br>The tests he had to endure were the worst. thing. ever. First he loses his glamour (SOOO SAD!!!!). Then he gets a conscience and nearly falls apart. (I cried a bit. I'm serious.) And then he experiences this horrible, sad fake-life with Meghan. (By then the tears were streaming down my face. I'm not even kidding. I cried.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413274ra/813488.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending was SO PERFECT. I was SO relieved that his glamour was back and that he wouldn't be aging (oh thank GOD). And then he said goodbye to Puck and they shook hands and I nearly started crying again, because a) they shook hands!!! and b) that would be the last time I'd ever see Puck. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413274ra/813489.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So despite everything Ash and Meghan got their happy ending. THANK GOD. <br><br><b>This book was incredible and perfect and terrible and awesome and an amazing adventure with characters you can't help but love. </b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2986853192" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2986853192" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30999560-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593744134p2/30999560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2986853192?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/30999560-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781459215337" href="/book/show/12418272-the-iron-knight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=disappointments">disappointments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=forgettable">forgettable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=trashy-pleasure">trashy-pleasure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=too-much">too-much</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=guilty-pleasure">guilty-pleasure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2986853192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10661611505679303369">Finally done! An achievement unlocked! Although, there are some side stories and a spin off series, but I am not going to touch any of those as I have already spent too much time on a series that was only mildly enjoyable and terribly written.<br/><br/>So, how did the last installment fare? Judging by my 2 stars, not very well, but let us start with the positives (+negatives)!<br/><br/>1. <b>THERE IS NO MEGHAN CHASE.</b> I cannot stress this enough, because despite Meghan's efforts to prove to us how different she is from</span>
  <span id="freeText10661611505679303369" style="display:none">Finally done! An achievement unlocked! Although, there are some side stories and a spin off series, but I am not going to touch any of those as I have already spent too much time on a series that was only mildly enjoyable and terribly written.<br /><br />So, how did the last installment fare? Judging by my 2 stars, not very well, but let us start with the positives (+negatives)!<br /><br />1. <b>THERE IS NO MEGHAN CHASE.</b> I cannot stress this enough, because despite Meghan's efforts to prove to us how different she is from every other girl, yet so ordinary, she is extremely cliche and boring. She always does what you expect her to do and most of the time, her POV is booooring. Instead, we have Ash as the main character which is of course better, if not for the fact that he is surrounded by a boring set of characters that always save him and always do the right thing and always have the answer and always and always and always. <br /><br />Of course, Grimalkin, the omniscient cat, is with them so you know they will never be lost in their quest to get Ash his soul. That alone already cuts more than half of the dangers they might face. But did they stop there? Oh no, they had to add to the fellowship a super strong "villain", Big Bad Wolf, who of course is their good ally in this case for reasons that were not entirely convincing plot-wise, so you know he was just there so they had even better chances of survival.<br /><br />2. Despite the problems with the cast, if you can somehow separate this book from its context (aka, Ash doing this for Meghan, etc.), there was a portion of the book that was perfectly enjoyable with characters going through trials. Definitely not the heart-stopping, never-finished trials the Guardian tried to convince us they were (they just weren't that hard for fey with powers and a brain), but some standard ones that the heros need to pass to get closer to their goal. There was a legitimate part that the characters' interactions and trial development was fun to actually read. Too bad that did not last long.<br /><br />3. Part of the ending was genuine in its storytelling, something really rare for this series and it proved to be even rarer when it late negated itself. Throughout the series, plot points, information, twists and even emotions and reactions are always conveniently placed as to have the "proper" conclusion. Therefore, a lot of what is happening falls flat and only makes me cringe more. However, there was a part with Ash exploring his potential human mortality that for once felt a bit more natural than the forced "happy ever after" or a cliffhanger that will lead to that "happy ever after" and it was really nice to read. I knew it would not last because of the writing, but I hoped that revelation of sorts would prove important for the ending. It did not. We got another extremely well placed happy ever after (because God forbid there is some relatability in the story).<br /><br />Unfortunately, that is all when it come to positives, but the negatives continue on. First of all: <b>THE ROMANCE.</b> <br /><br />If there is no Meghan in the book, where do we get our angsty romance dose? The answer is of course... the past. <i>His own love had died a horrible death, killing any gentler feelings the Winter prince might have had. Or so he thought.</i> Or sooo he thouuuught. Of course we had to invent a new triangle now (literally bringing it back from the grave) that Puck had stepped down from being a romantic rival and that there was virtually no Meghan around. Despite these characters living for hundreds of years, they all act like 7 year olds who just liked someone for the first time. Ash starts doubting his choices the moment he meets Ariella again and it has to be Ariella herself to lead him back to Meghan every time, even though she is also the one trying to steer him off. I mean, I don't know anymore. Ariella could easily be one of the most complicated characters, but she is reduced to a part of a convoluted triangle that was never a triangle to begin with and only serves the role of... serving Ash.<br /><br />Then, there is this whole idea of getting a soul. The series has tried explaining how Fey have no soul since they were born from human emotions/myths/etc so they cannot really feel or have any regrets, but... they do? THEY REALLY DO? Apparently it is easier to shut off that part of them, but it is there, as it is obvious from these 4 books, so the whole "human" understanding is kinda silly, since every main and important side character has gone through many, many, many, many emotions and thus it really does not bring anything new to the table when Ash is discovering how humans feel.<br /><br />I could write more in depth about every problem, but enough time has been wasted on this. Goodbye, Iron Fey series. I will never understand your popularity and I hope to deter even one person from ever picking you up! That would be my happy ever after!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10661611505679303369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1266305063" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1266305063" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1266305063?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1266305063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5607116726765490853">I thought <i>The Iron Queen</i> is bad enough, but it was before I read <i>The Iron Knight</i>...<br/><br/>Julie Kagawa herself revealed in the interview at the end of this book, that <i>The Iron Knight</i> was written because her editor convinced her Meghan and Ash should not be broken apart.<br/><br/>Shame on you, editor. <br/><br/>So what should Ms. Kagawa do in order to get Meghan and Ash back together? What should she do to give her editor and all the Ash/Meghan shippers the Happy Ever After they want? Let's do a checklist:<br/><br/>(1) Put Ash on a </span>
  <span id="freeText5607116726765490853" style="display:none">I thought <i>The Iron Queen</i> is bad enough, but it was before I read <i>The Iron Knight</i>...<br /><br />Julie Kagawa herself revealed in the interview at the end of this book, that <i>The Iron Knight</i> was written because her editor convinced her Meghan and Ash should not be broken apart.<br /><br />Shame on you, editor. <br /><br />So what should Ms. Kagawa do in order to get Meghan and Ash back together? What should she do to give her editor and all the Ash/Meghan shippers the Happy Ever After they want? Let's do a checklist:<br /><br />(1) Put Ash on a quest to find a way to become human.<br /><br />(2) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Get Ash's dead girlfriend to come back to life so she could help Ash to finish his tasks.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />(3) We need some plot development and fight scenes! Put Ash and everyone else to go to the End of the World...otherwise nothing would happen in this book!<br /><br />(4) Add A LOT OF ANGST and Ash carrying on about "Meghan I love you but you rejected me!!!!" whining into the story.<br /><br />(5) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Get Ash's supposedly dead girlfriend to make the final sacrifice for Ash so he can become human. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />(6) Let Ash grant his wish...<b>without having to pay any real price.</b><br /><br />There're a few more reasons why I think this book is awful, but I will mention them when I have time.<br /><br /><i>Edited @30/04/2015 10:00PM:</i><br /><br /><b>Warning: all-out ranting starts here, don't like don't read:</b><br /><br />Let's get down to business, shall we? First, let me tell you I didn't care much about Ash throughout the first three books, still I at least did think he is a decent love interest in Book 3 (Don't get me started with Book 1 and Book 2, I don't want to be reminded of Meghan's Too Stupid To Live, unreasonable lust with the mysterious ice prince) however it all changed after I read <i>The Iron Knight</i>.<br /><br />In <i>The Iron Queen</i>, Ash hinted to Meghan about his dark past, and in this Book 4, his part is revealed and oh, dear goodness it only shows me how much of a bastard he had been during his long immortal life! I know, Ms. Kagawa might probably want to use Ash's dark past and his quest for redemption as a plot device to give Ash more depth, to make him different from the other brooding, darkly handsome YA male love interests, but unluckily Ms. Kagawa seems to go overboard on this part.<br /><br />Well...I've read characters with dark past before, I've read characters redeeming themselves despite of their past wrongdoing. However, Ms. Kagawa had done TOO LITTLE to make Ash worthy enough for redemption. Supposedly Ash should go through three trials to proof himself and face his past mistakes, but in the end those trials are <i>nothing</i>, none of them is harsh nor torturous nor soul-shattering nor life-changing enough to prove Ash is indeed worthy of a soul.<br /><br />Those ridiculous trials aside (plus the story about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[how Ash's dead ex girlfriend is really not dead after all <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is just as ridiculous), Ash's backstory also makes one thing become clear: <b>the romance between Ash and Meghan makes no sense</b>. Although it's easy for me to understand why a TSTL little girl would fall in love with Ash, but on the other hand, <b>what has Ash ever seen in Meghan anyway? What makes him love her so much? What makes Meghan different from the other love-sicked human girls he toyed with and then dumped without a second thought?</b> The only explanation I can think of is: for the sake of driving the plot onward, Ash must fall in love with Meghan, so Ms. Kagawa just...<i>made</i> it happen, despite logic and reason and stuff. <br /><br />To add insult to injury, Ash never has to pay any real price to gain a soul <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[because conveniently enough his ex girlfriend paid the price for him <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. By the end of the book, it becomes clear that Ms. Kagawa created nothing but one plot convenience after another to make way for a Happy Ever After. <br /><br />The only problem is, does Ash deserve this HEA? Nap, in my opinion as TSTL as Meghan is, she still doesn't deserve to end up with a mass murderer (who obviously has never really confessed to her about his past wrongdoing). In my opinion, Ash should have been spending the next 100 years to redeem himself before he can win back the right of being with anyone else.<br /><br />You know what, not every YA book needs to have a Happy Ever After, The Darkangel trilogy doesn't, and it's freaking awful to create one plot convenience after another to make way for your HEA!<br /><br />But stupid me, what am I thinking? Of course Ash would be allowed to go back to Meghan ASAP in the end, of course Ash and Meghan would have their HEA, because it's what Kagawa's editor and her readers would want! This series is about wish-fulfilling and handsome boyfriends, just like most of the post-Twilight YA novels out there, it is not about realism, the art of storytelling and real redemption. Silly me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5607116726765490853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/938321110?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara (Freadom Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara (Freadom Library)" href="/user/show/24190242-sara-freadom-library">Sara (Freadom Library)</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13322765-the-iron-knight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer938321110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15229668266274064922">Actual rating 4.5 stars<br/><br/><b>Critically</b><br/> Plot - 4.5 out of 5 stars<br/>Really enjoyed it. It was exciting, action-packed, mysterious with a great mid-way plot twist and a very sweet and satisfying ending.<br/><br/> Writing Style - 4 out of 5 stars<br/>It's very simple but with very beautiful and detailed descriptions. Every time there is a POV change, there is a slight change to match the voice of the person. Within the story, there's a lot of foreshadowing to later plot points which are a bit easy to catch on to.<br/><br/> Charact</span>
  <span id="freeText15229668266274064922" style="display:none">Actual rating 4.5 stars<br /><br /><b>Critically</b><br /> Plot - 4.5 out of 5 stars<br />Really enjoyed it. It was exciting, action-packed, mysterious with a great mid-way plot twist and a very sweet and satisfying ending.<br /><br /> Writing Style - 4 out of 5 stars<br />It's very simple but with very beautiful and detailed descriptions. Every time there is a POV change, there is a slight change to match the voice of the person. Within the story, there's a lot of foreshadowing to later plot points which are a bit easy to catch on to.<br /><br /> Characters - 4 out of 5 stars<br />We get a new point of view in this book compared to the rest of the books in this series. Ash, one of the male protagonist in this series, takes center stage and becomes the main voice as he takes a journey for love. I liked getting the chance to get to know him better and more in depth in this book. He's strong and brave and determined. But he also shows a lot of vulnerability and openness that we hadn't seen from him before and it was really interesting to see the complexity of his character closer. He's torn about a lot of the possible decisions in his future and it was great to see him be a little on the weaker side throughout this book. We also get some of my lovable Puck, whom I love and who is one of my favorite characters of this series. <br /><br /><b>Emotionally</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was not expecting to like this book as much as I actually did.<br /><br />The plot was fascinating. The concept was really intriguing concept, the act of a faerie becoming human and what that would take. The journey itself was intense. We saw a lot more of the Nevernever than we have had before in the previous books. Some of them were really cool and interesting, and others were downright frightening and almost made me want to stop reading because I am huge chicken when it comes to scary things. There was an amazing plot twists in this book that blew me away! I had no idea that that was even possible, let alone to see it happen was crazy. It definitely improved the series for me because I was not expecting something like that at all. The group that forms for this book was actually hilariously disconnected. They didn't always get along and weren't necessarily the best of friends but it worked. The dynamics of the team helped Ash in his journey. Which was super intense and amazing by the way. I didn't realize how deep the author was going to get when she built the becoming a human journey, but it was very through and well thought out. There were so many different facets and it was an eye opening experience for me to see human nature from an outside point of view. <br /><br />Ash as a character was also fascinating. I didn't really connect with him very well in the first few books because of his cold personality and how we didn't really get to see his thought process. But in this book I could see into his head and his feelings and it was so much easier to connect and get to know him and overall feel for him and his predicament. It was so interesting to see his development from how he used to be, who he is at the moment of the journey and who he's trying to become for love. I didn't expect that much development in one book.<br /><br />Overall, this is a really fun and entertaining series. I'm really glad I read it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life">Donna {Book Passion For Life}</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life?shelf=ya-paranormal-romance">ya-paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162341249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9875098120755694545">Posted on: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bookpassionforlife.blogspot.com/'>http://bookpassionforlife.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><i>
  <b>"I’m almost there. Wait for me just a little bit longer."</b>
</i><br/><br/>I honestly don’t even know where to begin with this review and I don’t even think I could write a review that will do this book the praise it deserves but I will say this, The Iron Knight had everything I could have asked for and more. Julie Kagawa has utterly surpassed my expectations and blown all previous books away with her truly amazing writing, her creative imagination and her gif</span>
  <span id="freeText9875098120755694545" style="display:none">Posted on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookpassionforlife.blogspot.com/">http://bookpassionforlife.blogspot.com/</a><br /><br /><i>
  <b>"I’m almost there. Wait for me just a little bit longer."</b>
</i><br /><br />I honestly don’t even know where to begin with this review and I don’t even think I could write a review that will do this book the praise it deserves but I will say this, The Iron Knight had everything I could have asked for and more. Julie Kagawa has utterly surpassed my expectations and blown all previous books away with her truly amazing writing, her creative imagination and her gift for storytelling. Not only has she done a fantastic job with this novel but she has left me utterly speechless. Never have I felt so much joy and sadness for a book before but that’s what I’m left with. I’m left with Joy because it’s the most perfect ending to a fantastic series and sadness because it’s finally come to an end. Not only am I sad to be leaving these characters that I love but I am also sad that I didn’t get to spend more time with them as I wished. After only discovering this series a few months ago, I feel my time has come to an end too quickly. But, I do believe it was the best possible way because the excitement I had when I first started this series, is still with me now even though I’ve finished the final book. <br /><br />Looking back on all four books, I honestly would have been sad had it of ended with The Iron Queen therefore I am truly grateful to Julie to have continued on with the series and created another amazing piece of work. Ash has always been a favourite character of mine, I’ve loved him from the start and if it’s possible I think I love him that much more now. This story shows him in a completely different light, you get to see his deepest darkest secrets and somehow still manage to love him. Julie definitely did the right thing by doing this book from his point of view, I know it was sad to leave Meghan behind but she’s not truly forgotten. Honestly, if could rate The Iron Knight 10 out of 10 I would. This book is definitely my favourite out of the series and this series is definitely my favourite out of everything I’ve read.<br /><br />Thank you once again to Julie Kagawa for captivating us, compelling us and taking us all on this incredible journey with you. Even though the series has come to an end, it will truly not be forgotten and will be forever in our hearts. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9875098120755694545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4465363453831709024">This was a YA fantasy story, about Ash trying to find a way to be with Meghan in the Iron court.<br/><br/>I liked Ash in this, and I felt sorry for him too. It didn’t seem fair that he had to sacrifice so much to be with Meghan, when all he wanted to do was to love her and protect her. We also didn’t get much from Meghan at all in this book, which was quite a change. <br/><br/>The storyline in this was about Ash trying to become human so that he could return to Meghan and live with her in the Iron Realm, which requ</span>
  <span id="freeText4465363453831709024" style="display:none">This was a YA fantasy story, about Ash trying to find a way to be with Meghan in the Iron court.<br /><br />I liked Ash in this, and I felt sorry for him too. It didn’t seem fair that he had to sacrifice so much to be with Meghan, when all he wanted to do was to love her and protect her. We also didn’t get much from Meghan at all in this book, which was quite a change. <br /><br />The storyline in this was about Ash trying to become human so that he could return to Meghan and live with her in the Iron Realm, which required a journey and several tests. This was quite a fun adventure, and I liked learning more about both Ash’s history and future. <br /><br />The ending to this was a little confusing. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ So will Ash age and die like we saw? I thought that you couldn’t have a soul and be immortal, but that seemed to be what the story hinted at.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />7 out of 10<br /></span>

<div id="review_154966031" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154966031" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154966031?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who loved The Iron Fey series </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=fey">fey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-need-it-like-a-fat-kid-needs-cake">i-need-it-like-a-fat-kid-needs-cake</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-need-to-buy-this-book">i-need-to-buy-this-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154966031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12123153337149284327"><br/>***Please note: It's been a while since finishing this book and I did not include many details in this review. <br/><br/>Initial thoughts after finishing the book:<br/><br/>Somebody get Stephenie Meyer on the phone because <i>this</i> is how you add onto a trilogy without completely screwing your characters over. <i>This</i> is how you make a semi-insta-love relationship awesome. <i>This</i> is how you end a love triangle. And <i>this</i> is how you write a freakin' book! <br/><br/>4 stars seems too low and I think I love Iron Queen a little more (whic</span>
  <span id="freeText12123153337149284327" style="display:none"><br>***Please note: It's been a while since finishing this book and I did not include many details in this review. <br><br>Initial thoughts after finishing the book:<br><br>Somebody get Stephenie Meyer on the phone because <i>this</i> is how you add onto a trilogy without completely screwing your characters over. <i>This</i> is how you make a semi-insta-love relationship awesome. <i>This</i> is how you end a love triangle. And <i>this</i> is how you write a freakin' book! <br><br>4 stars seems too low and I think I love Iron Queen a little more (which I gave 5 stars). So actual rating is more like 4.5 stars. Full review to come!<br><br>Thoughts after some time had passed:<br><br>Wow, I can't believe I'm saying this, but this book didn't hold the same magic as books 1-3. Don't get me wrong, I still really enjoyed it, which is why I think it belongs with my 3.5 star books. <br><br>I am an Ash girl through and through. You cannot begin to imagine how excited I was to receive this as an ARC from Netgalley! I seriously did a major happy dance. <br><br><a href="http://s181.photobucket.com/albums/x95/shellnick2003/?action=view&amp;current=0e934fc2-42e6-4994-b588-fa95c05e4340.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347099ra/701444.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>In this installment, we find Ash set out on his final adventure: to travel to the End of the World to find a soul. Without one, he will never be able to step foot in the Iron realm. Besides Puck, Ash finds himself accompanied by a few surprise companions and of course, the Cat. This book seemed to be slower paced that the others, focusing mainly on a lot of character development. I think it's fair to say by the end of the book you will know as much about tAsh as you did about Meghan. And that's saying something considering she had three books in her POV and Ash has only one.<br><br>I gobbled this book up, attempting to savor every moment. As usual, the banter between Puck and Ash was awesome. Julie never disappoints with her character dialog. In this book we really got a chance to have a deeper understanding of Ash *and* Puck, which was a really nice bonus. We learn more about Ariella's death and Ash's vowel. We also get a chance to see just how much Ash loves Meghan. And he truly does since he travels to the End of the World for her. The world building was once again awesome. You could easily picture the scenes described.<br><br>So, why was I not feeling the magic as much? I think a big part was because I really missed Meghan. I didn't realize how much she shaped Ash as a character in this series until she wasn't a major player. She does make some appearances in this book, but this is virtually *Ash's* book, told by his POV. <br><br>The ending was a happy one, but I think I prefer the ending in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8685612.The_Iron_Queen__Iron_Fey___3_" title="The Iron Queen (Iron Fey, #3) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Queen</a> instead because it was just a very emotional ending. <i>The Iron Knight</i> did have me tear up a bit, but <i>The Iron Queen</i> opened the flood gates. <br><br>So, if you loved the Iron Fey series definitely give <i>The Iron Knight</i> a go!<br><br>More reviews and more at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12123153337149284327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_130039811" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130039811" />
    <a title="Krystle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle"><img alt="Krystle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403921272p2/2639204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130039811?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystle" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle">Krystle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130039811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7020593452099431409">I have finally reached the end of this series. Finally. Let’s just say I’m just a masochist and I just had to find out how this damn things ends especially if I came this far. Hah.<br/> <br/>The plot of this book was so predictable and dry. And that whole End of the World thing? Reminds me of the final bosses in the early Final Fantasy series. Yeah, call me not impressed. Everything seems so rehashed and overdone.<br/> <br/>Do you remember what I said in my previous review?<br/> <br/><i>“But anyway, the ending while actually re</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7020593452099431409" style="display:none">I have finally reached the end of this series. Finally. Let’s just say I’m just a masochist and I just had to find out how this damn things ends especially if I came this far. Hah.<br /> <br />The plot of this book was so predictable and dry. And that whole End of the World thing? Reminds me of the final bosses in the early Final Fantasy series. Yeah, call me not impressed. Everything seems so rehashed and overdone.<br /> <br />Do you remember what I said in my previous review?<br /> <br /><i>“But anyway, the ending while actually resolved makes me mad because obviously it’s open ended and now there’s gonna be another book from ASH’S POINT OF VIEW! Watch I bet it’s all gonna be about omg, Puck that evil bastard killed my ex-girlfriend, then omg, Meghan I love and misses you so much and we needs to have more hot loving time, but NO YOU REJECTED ME.”</i><br /> <br />Totally happened in this book! Lots of angsting, and then more angsting, and then can you guess? ANGSTING! …With a side dose of an action scene here and there. I’m really sick of how the whole cold-hearted and emotionally absent people in stories later turn out to be such saps – which is what Ash became. A freaking overly emotional sap.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He spent the majority of the time bemoaning his faerie heritage and how he needs to be with Meghan, and then a sudden onslaught of “OH! What about my first love?” which brings up another round of somberness in our ice-prince because he relives all his hurt emotions and thus ensuing the Puck hating. This book could not be more predictable.<br /> <br />And then guess who shows up? GUESS! That’s right, ASH’S EX! Gee, who woulda thunk it? How transparent can this story get? Oh, and it’s really annoying how she’s basically a plot device to add “tension” to the book when I really felt none because her role in the book in the story will only end up one way – GONE. Yes, we are so convinced Ash is torn between his old flame and the new one when, you know, her tragic past, annoyingly obvious foreshadowing hints, and lack of an actual personality make it so easy to connect to her.<br /><br />The witty comments that are supposed to be so funny from all the characters felt so... I don't know familiar? Like they've been used elsewhere and didn't feel "new". Everything had a sort of been there, done that type of reaction that I really wonder what source material she got her inspiration from.<br /><br />I totally hate how all the other supporting characters are basically the same mold as they were when you first meet them. Grimalkin, especially, is the same pompous, cowardly, unloyal guide who <i>always</i> seems to have the answers for everything and never gets into trouble himself. How boring and lazy. Whatever.<br /> <br />The only part of the book I mildly liked is when Ash has to experience life as a mortal together with Meghan who is immortal. Many books actually have this conflict but we never ever see it played out because an answer is found for the leading couple without having to go through the trouble of experiencing this. But in this book we get to see this happen and feel his shame, resentment, and hurt when he grows old and frail while the rest of his family stays young and beautiful. I thought this was pretty nifty and fun but then, you know, it would get in the way our couple’s happy ending so this is totally not gonna happen.<br /> <br />I don’t get how it’s a sacrifice for him to give up his immortality to be with Meghan if he gets to LIVE FOREVER ANYWAY. WTHELL?! Pfft! Lame! No thanks. And I thought it was super annoying to be in Meghan’s head – nuh uh, Ash is way worse.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Fail in all ways. Just fail. Do. Not. Want.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7020593452099431409" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_172996429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172996429" />
    <a title="Louize" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3019973-louize"><img alt="Louize" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348845553p2/3019973.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172996429?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Louize" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Louize" href="/user/show/3019973-louize">Louize</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3019973-louize?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172996429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16572813935249785514">After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12151437.The_Iron_Queen__Iron_Fey___3_' title='The Iron Queen (Iron Fey, #3) by Julie Kagawa' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Iron Queen</a>, I remember saying that I was glad seeing Meghan mature. This time, it’s Ash’s turn… <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“I promised I’d find a way for us to be together, I intend to keep that promise.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>I should have read the <u>Survival Guide to the Nevernever</u> first before I prowled into the book. <b>Iron Knight</b> is a non-stop action/adventure. Ash is so serious in keeping his promise that he was willing to go through everything as quickly as he should, and travel the extra mile needed to gain a soul. A v</span>
  <span id="freeText16572813935249785514" style="display:none">After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12151437.The_Iron_Queen__Iron_Fey___3_" title="The Iron Queen (Iron Fey, #3) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Queen</a>, I remember saying that I was glad seeing Meghan mature. This time, it’s Ash’s turn… <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I promised I’d find a way for us to be together, I intend to keep that promise.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I should have read the <u>Survival Guide to the Nevernever</u> first before I prowled into the book. <b>Iron Knight</b> is a non-stop action/adventure. Ash is so serious in keeping his promise that he was willing to go through everything as quickly as he should, and travel the extra mile needed to gain a soul. A very impatient young man, he doesn’t like wasting time indeed. He left me breathless and proud.<br /><br />Again, the brilliance of Ms. Julie in choosing characters is superb. This book has the best party-of-five for this adventure. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The daring Prince of Winter Court, Ash; the Summer Court jester, Puck; the cait sith, Grimalkin; the Big Bad Wolf; and Ariella. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The exchange of wits and lines was very entertaining; there was never a dull moment. It was the roughness of their individualities that made the chemistry of characters smooth.<br /><br />The setting is the second brilliant factor. From the River of Dreams (through the Deep Wyld and the Briars and then the gauntlet) to the End of the World, the description and vividness of imagination was flawless. It was the perfect blend for the intention of the adventure. Anything less is unacceptable.<br /><br />It was also interesting how morality was applied into the story. Often, when we speak of gaining a soul, we speak of morality. Something so pure is not easily won. But there is no preaching on the matter. Simply that, having a soul doesn’t make us good; it makes us remember our offenses and vowing to live better in the future. That factor alone leveled up YA fiction.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I am still yours, my queen,” Ash said looking me straight in the eye. “If you’ll have me.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Finally, I’m happy that this was told from Ash’s point of view. I believe that the ending of the series was very powerful and effective because of that.<br /><br />Congratulations Ms. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2995873.Julie_Kagawa" title="Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie Kagawa</a>, and thank you for the wonderful journey through the world of <b>Iron Fey</b>. <br /><br /><i>*Thanks to Harlequin and NetGalley for the egalley.</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16572813935249785514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13145894090590328268" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>What's this review?</b>
</u><br>See, I was going to write a real review for that one and not a compilation of my <s>rambling</s> thoughts but thanks to wonderful girls, there's a badge Kat created to add a little love in this GR world and to show that we can write great reviews without spamming the hell of everyone. <br><br>I chose <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/885205335?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Chelsea's review</a> because she perfectly captured what I felt reading this book... and because she's an amazing friend. Go read her review people &lt;3<br><br><b>So, Chelsea, you're famous ma belle &lt;3 and you fucking deserves it.</b> <s>and yeah I know you're on your honeymoon, such a time to make a star of you ;D</s> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421354344i/13364675.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>________________________<br><b>Initial non-review <i>aka</i> I don't have the time to write a real review</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420164411i/13184651._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"What do you think?"<br>He bared his fangs at me. "Be careful, boy. In some tales, the hero gets eaten by the monster after all."</b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>What a quest!</b> That was the most excruciating and tiring of all these outstanding books, and yet, <b>exactly what I wanted</b>. See, I have a thing : <br>although I can <i>adore</i> a world, the beautiful writing which brings it to live, a fast-paced plot and stunning twists, yet multi-layered characters <b>always</b> stay my undoing. <br><br>Closing <i>The Iron Knight</i>, there's only single thing I want to say, and that's <i>Thank you, Julie Kagawa.</i> Thank you to have brilliantly managed to create such <b>an incredible <i>flawed</i> character</b>. <br><br>Who am I talking about? <b>Ash of course.</b><br><br>Ash who has an agenda, who's willing to respect his promise : to find a way to live in the Iron realm. In this quest, he will be spared <i>nothing</i> : fear, loneliness, regret, hate of himself, and above all that - <b>courage to hope and to go on. To love. To overtake his past, to accept his weaknesses, to be <i>whole</i> again.</b><br><br>Oh, Ash, you made me <i>so proud.</i><br><br><i>Full review to come - Just know that this world won a special place in my heart, and as always in this case, I'm let both happy and a bit empty as well.</i></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fICl9bSWu5q8OlqGG1nBYhjj7QI/1nSD/gMFG+nE3LhGpswnD8hy8hsR7ufsrMu9zrwKyvFb+uSlfUOqJIcuIg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZPxnHpga4Td2q4smo90htlz1iSmtRy6Re7bhV6ODDqFe2g7MI0QoX9GAP0dUKCtpiqpu4WPKoPYgyKfmbsD8Ow==')})
  }
//]]>
